-1d20-
1. Ring of Druthwid’s Defense
Appearance: Itis a band of solid iron, wrought witha
simple scale pattern. It was clearly made for someone 7 Ts
with very large hands. When worn, the ring stains the ff 0
wearer's skin a deep green. E 0
Enchantment: The Ring of Druthwid's Defense allows (E 7
the user to summon a circle of large, magical kite 2 J]
shields that rotate slowly around the user, creating a Nay, JY
solid barrier and protecting them from all attacks for =
10 minutes. Can be used once per day.
History: Druthwid was a paladin, born more than five hundred years
ago. Not much is known about the mysterious man, but legend says he
died in battle, giving his life to protect the head priest of his church. The
priest, in honor of his fallen friend, created the Ring of Druthwid’s
Defense, which was passed from one head priest to the next until it was
stolen.
2. Ringblade
Appearance: A simple ring of black metal. A small ‘X' has been carved
on the inside of the band.
Enchantment: When slipped onto one finger, the ring grows into a
knife, short sword or longsword, depending on the users preference.
The sword is the same black metal as the ring, and a low hum seems to
emanate from the blade. Unless the ring is taken from their finger, the
user cannot be disarmed.
History: This ring once belonged to a well-known royal who had a
hobby of moonlighting as an equally well-known highwayman. He
would wear this ring on a necklace during the day, and spill blood with
it by night. However, the royal rogue was killed when an operation went
wrong, and his belongings were auctioned by his shamed family.
2

----------------------

###PAGE:12###
3. Penelope's Ring of Time Reversal

Appearance: A slightly discolored and dirty ring made of intertwining
silver threads. The ring feels fragile and old, as if it could fall apart at
any moment.
Enchantment: This ring allows the user to turn back time five minutes.
Only the user is aware of the magic, and only they retain memories of
the time that was overwritten. The ring disintegrates after one use.
History: Saint Penelope was a wizard who dedicated her life to her
research of the arcane. Legend says she found answers to immortality
and time-reversal, but she died before she could share her research with
the world. Her artifacts are highly sought-after, as they always contain
strong - if delicate and disaster-prone - enchantments.

4. Ring of the Martyr
Appearance: A delicate golden ring with a
clear diamond setin the center. Inside the gem 3
is a roiling cloud of mist that swirls and (£222;
presses against the barriers of the diamond, #2”
struggling to escape. 1
Enchantment: A living soul is sealed within
the gem. Whenever the wearer is dealt a
‘mortal wound, the spirit inside of the ring dies
in the user's place. The spirit in the gem
can be replaced, but only by a willing soul.
History: This ring was created for Lile Erstwhile, a fearsome mercenary
known for her cruel and merciless ways. In a legendary battle between
Lile and her estranged sister Mile, Lile was defeated and the ring cut
from her hand. The ring was lost for many decades before turning up in
an auction house.

###PAGE:13###
5. Possessed Ring (Paracelcius the Wizard)
Appearance: A dainty band of silver etched with flowering vines.
Enchantment: This ring is possessed by the spirit of Paracelcius the
Wizard. This wizard, though resigned and somewhat depressed, is
capable of identifying any magical artifact as long as the user can
accurately describe it.

History: Paracelcius was a court wizard in the service of the king for
many, many years. As he grew older, Paracelcius grew bored with his
day-to-day tasks and decided to experiment with immortality, which
resulted in his spirit being sealed into a ring he was wearing at the time.
6. Ring of Elemental Charge
Appearance: A set of three interlocking rings,
each set with a small ruby, sapphire and amber.
Enchantment: When worn, this ring imbues any
weapon held in the same hand with either fire,
frost, or electricity damage based on the user's
preference. Once per day, the user can change the
elemental effect.
History: This ring was once split into three separate parts - each one
belonged to a high knight of the Circle of the Oak - a world-renowned
mercenary guild. When the guild was disbanded, the rings were
scattered throughout the realm. A historian spent much of his career
hunting down the three rings and joining them together once again
before selling them to a collector.
7. North-South Ring - Cursed
Appearance: A gold band etched with two opposing arrows.
Enchantment: When this ring is worn, the wearer fully believes that
north is to the south. Nothing can be said or done to convince the wearer
otherwise. Once donned, the user becomes very possessive of the ring -
they will not willingly take it off.
4

###PAGE:14###
History: The exact history of this ring is not known. Legend has it that
a hedge mage, tired of her cruel husband coming home from work every
day, crafted this befuddling ring. She slipped it on her husband's finger
and he became so lost that he never came home.
8. Ring of Uncomfortable Odds
Appearance: A heavy brass ring with a large, \
pyramidal citrine set in the center. |

seems to glow, absorbing light and heat
throughout the day. When the gem is full, the

11. Ring of Detachment
Appearance: A ring in the shape of a tiny blade, ~~
bent back on itself to form a band. rg
Enchantment: This ring allows the user to easily \
and painlessly remove and reattach the hand that \
wears the ring. The user retains complete control
of the hand for up to 60 feet. If the ring is
removed, the hand acts as if it has been severed
and is unable to be reattached.
History: This ring was created by a court wizard who enjoyed pranks a
little too much. A legendary thief saw the potential in the ring, and stole
it for her own nefarious purposes. When the thief died, she passed it on
to her daughter, who followed in her mother’s footsteps.

###PAGE:16###
12. Ring of Apparent Death
Appearance: A ring molded in the shape of two clasped hands.
Enchantment: The wearer instantly falls
into a magical sleep. Their heartbeat slows,
their skin grows cold and, for all intents and A
purposes, the wearer appears dead. While in ZS
this state, the wearer does not need to
breathe, eat or drink. The user can exist in
this state for thirty days before they begin to
die. The wearer is not capable of removing -
the ring themselves.
History: No one knows exactly where this ring came from, or why it was
created.
13. Ring of Unnecessary Introductions

Appearance: A simple silver band, stamped with the letter ‘M.
Enchantment: Allows the wearer to magically and instantaneously
know the name of any humanoid within eyesight.
History: This ring was crafted as a joke gift for a young noble with a
habit of forgetting names. A few years passed, then he pawned it to
repay his gambling debts.

14. Headache Ring
Appearance: A golden band set with a cloudy green gem.
Enchantment: This ring gives the wearer the appearance of being ill,
with the severity of the illness completely up to the user. The effects are
entirely aesthetic, and disappear the moment the ring is removed.
However, there is a 10% chance the user will truly fall ill, and that the
illness will remain after the ring is removed.
History: This ring was created by a court wizard who hated attending
social gatherings. She would slip the ring on, fall ll, and refuse to join
the celebrations. On one such occasion, however, the ring backfired and
she contracted a terrible disease that ended her life.

7

###PAGE:17###
15. Ring of Alarm
Appearance: A copper wire ring with a green stone nestled in the
center.
Enchantment: The user can set the ring to let out a loud sound,
alarming them whenever certain conditions are met. Such conditions
can include: at a certain time of day, whenever a living creature gets
within a certain distance, when a specific door is opened, etc. A
maximum of three conditions may be set.
History: A young warlock created this ring after he slept through many
of his morning classes. The ring soon became a popular commodity, and
he went on to make dozens of these rings for his fellow students.

from their mouth at will. It is an unpleasant experience that has a 30%
chance of causing the user to choke.

18. Backlash Ring
Appearance: A slender silver band with a small mirror setin the center.
Enchantment: For 1d10 minutes, any magic cast at the wearer is
reflected back on the caster. Must be charged under the light of the full
‘moon between uses.
History: This ring was created by famous duelist, Matthew Strongeye.
After being thrashed repeatedly, his rivals gathered together and
ambushed him in the road, stealing his Backlash Ring and leaving him
beaten and bloodied in the ditch. Since then, the ring has been a coveted
artifact by many spellcasters over the years.
19. Ring of Light
Appearance: A silver ring with a large white stone set in the middle.
Enchantment: When activated, the gem emits a bright beam of white
light in a 60ft. cone.
History: This ring was given as a gift to the TR
kingdom's most prodigious explorer, Onisha SS
Steadyfoot. A few years ago, Steadyfoot went
missing after heading into a newly unearthed cave
that was later discovered to be infested with
goblins. Her body was never recovered, but her =
maps, journals and belongings were discovered a
‘hidden away in a goblin den.
20. Ring of Forgery
Appearance: A golden ring wrought in the shape of a delicate quill.
Enchantment: Allows the wearer to perfectly emulate another's
handwriting. The user must first see an example of the handwriting they
wish to copy, but the end result is nearly infallible.
History: This ring was owned by Hillicus Forge, a famous forger known
for tricking the bank out of thousands of gold pieces. His ruse was
eventually discovered, however, and he was killed when the city guard
raided his home. His possessions were sold in auction.

22. Amulet of Breath
Appearance: A rough piece of teal sea glass on a simple chain.
Enchantment: The user can simply pop this amulet in their mouth, and
the magic will allow them to go without breath for thirty minutes. The
amulet must be charged for thirty minutes in clean air between uses.
History: Once upon a time, there lived a beautiful maiden destined to
be married to someone she did not love. Instead of marrying, she threw
herself off the cliffs and into the sea. Legend has it that the sea found her
too beautiful to drown, and so slipped a magical stone under her tongue
50 that she could swim safely to a faraway land.

23. Amulet of Thrumar’s Navigation
Appearance: A small glass orb dangling from a rusted brass chain, with
a small ball of moss rolling around inside.
Enchantment: When activated inside of a cave, mine, dungeon or
similar underground structure, the ball of moss inside the amulet will
roll around in the sphere, leading the user towards the closest
accessible exit.
History: This amulet was created by a dwarven miner named Thrumar.
His fellow dwarves laughed at him for carrying such a bauble. A few
months later, Thrumar was the only dwarf to escape with his life after a
tunnel collapsed.
24. Sooth-Song Amulet
Appearance: A wide band of carved bone, threaded onto a necklace of
braided twine.
Enchantment: When swung in a fast circle on its chain, this amulet
emits a high-pitched sound that has a calming, soothing effect on those
that hear it. It reduces anger, fear and other forms of agitation, magical
or natural. The stronger the emotion, however, the less likely the
creature is to be calmed.
History: This amulet was created by a farmer, many hundreds of years
ago, to sooth her animals during thunderstorms. Her cattle loved her
dearly, and some say she even had a touch of druidic magic.
25. Amulet of Warmth
Appearance: A small glass globe on a leather strap. A small flame
flickers gently inside.
Enchantment: This amulet keeps the wearer at a comfortably warm
temperature, on even the coldest nights, and the user is not affected by
frost-based spells.
History: This amulet was crafted by the Arch-Wizard of the Mage
College for her wife, who always seemed to be cold.
12

----------------------

###PAGE:22###
26. Amulet of Clear Breath
Appearance: A heavy golden torc, wrought in the shape of an elegant,
twisting vine.
Enchantment: While worn, the user cannot be choked, strangled or
suffocated by physical or magical means.
History: Once, many years ago, there was a young noble man named
Flavio Olgard. After he nearly died choking on a piece of salmon, he had
this necklace crafted so he might never experience that again.
27. Amulet of Rest
Appearance: A small crescent moon amulet, set with glittering gems on
asilver chain.
Enchantment: Once per week, the wearer can summon this amulets
magic and instantly gain the benefits of a long rest. This amulet must be
charged under the crescent moon between uses.
History: This amulet was created by a student of the Mage College who
needed more time to study. After she passed all her classes, she gave the
necklace to her apprentice who, in turn, gave it to his apprentice.
28. Necklace of the Wolf Moon
Appearance: A large canine tooth stained with age, dangling from a
rough leather strap.
Enchantment: Allows the user to polymorph into a wolf at will
However, there is a 5% chance the user will forget themselves and
become feral, in which case the user must be forcibly returned to their
original shape or remain a wolf forever.
History: Legend says this tooth was pulled from the mouth of Olric
Stoutfur, a famous werewolf who terrorized the countryside hundreds
of years ago. A powerful paladin finally took Olric down and pulled the
tooth from his mouth, fashioning it into a pendant without realizing the
magic it held. When the full moon came, the paladin was transformed
into a wolf, and his mind was lost to madness.

29. Amulet of Distracted Gaze
Appearance: A large, spherical ruby set in a golden
clasp. (0)
Enchantment: This amulet distracts all those that
look upon the wearer. As long as they are strangers, X
no one the user interacts with will remember their i!
face. \
History: This amulet was created by a monk, who
wished to walk the world as a stranger. For five
years the monk lived without friends, family or
relationships of any kind, and meditated on the
meaning of interpersonal connections. When his |
pilgrimage was completed, he gave the amuletto his
temple and published a very profound book on his a
findings.
30. Pendant of Feline Friendship
Appearance: A large feline claw etched with geometric designs,
dangling from a rough leather strap.
Enchantment: Allows the wearer to communicate fluently with all
feline creatures. Cats, panthers, lions and other such cats will behave
amicably towards the wearer, and are more likely to aid the user when
called upon.
History: This amulet was commissioned by a rat-hunter by the name of
Antoinette Coldwater. With the aid of the pendant’s magic and her
hoard of trained cats, she grew to fame as the most accomplished rat-
hunter in the kingdom. After a rough encounter with a diseased rat,
Coldwater fell ill and perished, and the majority of her belongings were
sold.

31. Necklace of Dahlia’s Voice
Appearance: A choker of black ribbon, dotted with tiny diamonds.
Enchantment: Gives the wearer an undeniably beautiful singing voice.
History: A long time ago, there was an elf named Dahlia. She had the
finest voice in the kingdom, and she traveled far and wide to sing for the
kings and queens of the world. A necklace of black ribbon was given to
her by one such king, an admirer of hers, and she wore it until the day
she died. Some say the magic of her voice infused the necklace,
bestowing her gift upon anyone who wears it.

32. Gimblette's Amulet of Bug Blasting
Appearance: A small green stone on a silver chain. The faint scent of
eucalyptus emanates from the smooth gem.
Enchantment: Insects and arachnids of any type or size cannot get
within five feet of the wearer. If a bug does happen to get past the
barrier, it explodes loudly and violently.
History: These pendants are not rare in the southern and more
temperate territories, and can be found scattered through the cities.
This one in particular was handmade by a witch, who was tired of
mosquitos bothering her as she harvested plants by moonlight.

33. Amulet of Insect Interaction
Appearance: A large pendant of amber with a beautiful black beetle set
inside. It dangles from a brass chain.
Enchantment: Allows the user to communicate fluently with insects
and arachnids. Flies, spiders, ants and other bugs will behave amicably
towards the wearer, and are more likely to aid the user when called
upon.
History: Once there was a ranger by the name of Galewind Grass, who
was famous across the kingdom for his ability to track even the most
elusive prey. He spent most of his days in the wilderness, traveling here
and there with no company besides his own. But this life was terribly
lonely, and so he asked the druids to give him an enchantment, allowing
him to speak to the wildlife around him.

34. Candle-Snuffer

Appearance: A silver candle-snuffer on a chain. The metal is blackened
with years of grime and candle smoke.
Enchantment: Allows the user to instantly extinguish small lanterns,
candles, torches or other kinds of light, magical or otherwise, as long as
they are within eyesight. Large flames such as campfires cannot be
extinguished.
History: Originally created for the butler of a noble house, this magical
candle-snuffer was stolen by a ring of amateur thieves, who quickly saw
its potential and put it to use for their own nefarious purposes.

36. Amulet of Good Health
Appearance: A silver tore, fashioned with delicate leaves and vines in
the likeness of a laurel wreath.
Enchantment: While this necklace is worn, the user cannot fall ill by
normal means - though the wearer is still fallible to magical illness and
poisons.
History: There was once an aging wizard. His granddaughter was often
ill and it was clear her days were numbered. The wizard searched
desperately for the magic to cure her and finally, after many long years
of research, he crafted this necklace. The girl flourished and lived a long
and happy life, with her grandfather's magic keeping her safe.

37. Amulet of Silence - Cursed
Appearance: A heavy golden pendant, carved with the image of a finger
pressed over hushed lips, threaded on a black ribbon.
Enchantment: While worn, the wearer loses the ability to speak. The
user cannot make any sort of sound including speaking, singing, sighing,
laughing, and so on. Once donned, this cursed item can only be removed
by the last person the wearer spoke to.
History: Once there was a noble woman with a terrible secret - a
terrible secret that was witnessed by her young serving boy. The noble
woman gave to him a necklace that took away his voice, so that he would
never speak of what he saw and, being illiterate, he had no way to betray
her. The necklace remained on the boy's neck until he grew old and
finally perished, the noble’s secret dying with him. To this day, no one
knows what he saw.
38. Amulet of Easy Return
Appearance: A silver pendant etched with the image of a cabin with
smoke pouring from the chimney, dangling from a silver chain.
Enchantment: While wearing this amulet, the wearer can mark their
location. From then on, once per day, the user can teleport back to the
marked location. All living things in contact with the wearer are also
teleported.
History: There was once a wizard named Odwin Marks, who had to
walk very far to work each day. Eventually he tired of his daily treks,
and he crafted two Amulets of Easy Return. One would teleport him to
‘work and the other would take him home. Eventually the wizard grew
old and retired - so he sold the amulets.
39. Choker of Choking - Cursed
Appearance: A simple choker of red ribbon, with a silver clasp.
Enchantment: This necklace tightens and strangles the wearer
whenever the command word is spoken. Can only be removed when a
second command word is spoken.
18

----------------------

###PAGE:28###
History: A long time ago, there was an assassin who was trained in the
art of enchantment. She had many pieces of jewelry that were the tools
of her vicious trade. However, one day, her little brother saw this lovely
necklace and put in on, unaware of its true use. He choked to death and,
upon finding his body, the assassin immediately swore off killing and
sold her tools.
40. Amulet of the Heart
Appearance: A small porcelain heart on a golden chain.
Enchantment: When worn, this amulet is warm to the touch, and gently
pulses with the heartbeat of the person of the wearer’s choosing.
History: This amulet was created by a potter, who was often traveling
away from his family. He gave it to his daughter, so the little girl could
always feel her father’s heart beating close to her own.

41. Cuffs of Hell's Strength
Appearance: A pair of wide cuffs made from shining steel. The metal is
etched with rows of geometric triangles. This bracelet causes the veins
in the wearer’s hands to glow faintly red.
Enchantment: Greatly increases the wearer's strength, allowing them
to perform great feats of physical ability. Such feats include bending
iron bars, lifting impossible amounts, and throwing objects huge
distances
History: These cuffs were worn by famous gladiator, Isabelle “Bone-
Pulper” Desani. Her ruse wasn't discovered until after she took her
‘winning riches and retired to the countryside. After her death, her cuffs
were sold at a high price to a memorabilia collector.
42. Bracelet of Dexterity
Appearance: A simple bracelet of gold, set with six circular garnets.
Enchantment: Greatly increases the wearer's dexterity. The user
becomes adept at instrument playing, lockpicking, acts of sleight of
hand, and so on.
History: This bracelet was commissioned by Darren Finethread, a well-
known tapestry weaver. As he grew old, his aching hands and gnarled
joints made it harder for him to practice his craft, and his condition grew
worse with each passing day, but with the magic of this bracelet,
Finethread was able to continue his passion of weaving beautiful
tapestries until his dying day.

43. Cuffs of Dwarven Skin
Appearance: Rough cuffs of braided iron.
Enchantment: The wearer's forearms and hands become completely
impervious to heat. Their skin becomes tough, and they become able to
handle sharp objects such as jagged metal, glass and razor-sharp blades
without fear of cutting themselves.
History: These cuffs were made by Torren Bladecutter, a reclusive
mage and blacksmith. She crafted these cuffs so she could handle red-
hot blades with her bare hands, which let her ‘feel the metal sing’. That,
she claims, is why her blades were so fine.

45. Molgmar’s Phantom Limb
Appearance: A simple bracelet made from shining black stone, etched
with golden runes.
Enchantment: This bracelet creates a fully-functioning phantom
replacement for the user's lost limb. The ghostly appendage functions
as normal and feels fully solid, even though it appears faintly pale and
transparent. The phantom limb is icy to the touch. If the user has no
missing limbs, this bracelet has no effect.
History: Long ago, there was a renowned dwarven warrior named
Moglmar. When he lost his axe-brandishing arm to a goblin captain in a
ferocious duel, he begged the gods to give him back his fighting prowess.
When he awoke the next day, this bracelet was around his wrist.
46. Cuffs of the Dual Duelist
Appearance: Two wide cuffs made from copper. The metal is covered
in simple chiseled lines.
Enchantment: Makes the user's off-hand just as useful as their
dominant hand - the user becomes truly ambidextrous, and takes no
disadvantages for duel-wielding.
History: These cuffs were created by Titania Sharpsteel - a renowned
dualist. She became iconic for her unique duel-wielding fighting
technique, which she used to take the pride and purses of many who
wished to challenge her.
47. Bracelet of Less Loss
Appearance: A narrow bracelet made of interlocking silver bands.
Enchantment: While wearing this bracelet, nothing can be removed
from the user's person without their explicit permission. This includes
clothing and items such as coins, jewelry and weapons.

###PAGE:32###
History: This bracelet was created by a mad hedge-mage named
Herman, who insisted on carrying his secret recipes and spells on his
person at all times, so his “valuable” inventions could never be stolen
and copied. His fears were realized when his spell books were stolen
while he was in the bath.

48. Cuff of Covert Passage
Appearance: A stained bracelet of braided leather with a brass buckle.
Enchantment: While wearing this bracelet, the user leaves behind no
footprints, fingerprints, scent trails, or other signs that could be used to
track them.
History: This bracelet was hastily created by Dewford Hillhorn, a
ranger who was forced to flee the country after poaching many of the
King’s prized hunting stock.

49. Cuffs of Connection

Appearance: Two golden bracelets, inlaid with twin rubies.
Enchantment: These bracelets are clearly designed to be worn by two
people. While worn, each person is always aware of the other's exact
location and well-being.
History: Long ago, there was a young a lord who was forced to leave his
newly-wedded wife and fight on the front lines of war. He
commissioned these bracelets so that she would always know that he
was alive and safe. When the war was over, he returned home to his wife
and the two lived a long and happy life together.

51. Cuff of the Criminal - Cursed

Appearance: A wide, heavy cuff of blackened iron.
Enchantment: This cuff can only be removed by the person who put it
on. It appears to be a simple cuff ~ however, when the command word
is spoken, the cuff suddenly weighs 500 Ibs, forcing the wearer to the
ground until the command word is spoken again. If spoken by the
wearer, the command word has no effect.
History: Hundreds of these were created over the years, and many jails
and prisons use such handcuffs to this day. This cuff was worn by Olfred
Direstone, a man who was in prison for life after killing his wife. He
spent months training and when the time came, he was able to escape,
hauling the immensely heavy handcuff with him.

52. Bracelet of the Gardener
Appearance: A delicate golden chain, dangling with glowing emeralds.

Enchantment: The user becomes very adept at the keeping and caring
of plants. They are also able to accurately identify common wild flora,
and how to harvest them.
History: Once there was a woman named Garland Strand, but she was
known as ‘The Flower Whisperer’ to those that knew her for her
unmatched gardening skills. She wore this bracelet while tending to her
luscious garden. Legend has it that the emeralds in this bracelet
absorbed her talent, passing it on to whoever wears it.

74. Mind-Search Earring
Appearance: A single teardrop-shaped diamond, hanging from an
ornate silver hook.
Enchantment: Once per day, the user can lay their hands on a

was tilling the ancient battlefield for planting season, and it was sold for
much less than it was worth.

75. Possessed Earrings (Twinkle the Thief)
Appearance: A set of small spherical amethysts hanging from silver

lockpicking, robbery, and other such clandestine objectives.

History: Twinkle the Gnome was a robber, well-known in the local
thieves guild. There was an old wizard in town that Twinkle would often
rob, selling his expensive potion supplies to the pawn shop. One day, she
decided to rob the wizard as usual, but the wizard had other plans. As
soon as she set foot in the door, the wizard's traps blew her body to
smithereens and sealed her soul into a chunk of amethyst. He carved the
stone into a pair of earrings and, as punishment, sold her to the very
pawn-shop she sold his ingredients to.

81. Circlet of the Sturdy Mind
Appearance: An elegant circlet of silver with a triangular emerald set
in the middle.
Enchantment: While this circletis worn, the user's mind cannot be read
and they are not affected by magical enchantments such as fear, charm,
sleep, or any spells that would alter the user's mental state.
History: Many years ago, there was a mercenary named Gulmar
Ol'Gresh. A local town hired him to slay an enchantress responsible for
burning their fields, so he set off in search of her. He found her but,
before Gulmar could even draw his sword, the enchantress laid a spell
over his mind. Crazy with spell-induced madness, Gulmar returned to
the town and killed half the town before his mind cleared. Seeing what
he had done, Gulmar fled the kingdom and commissioned this circlet.
He wore it until the day of his death.

50 that no evil could stand before her without quaking.

85. Circlet of the Crow Queen
Appearance: A rugged crown made of black feathers and copper wire.
Enchantment: Allows the user to polymorph into a crow at will.
History: This circlet was worn by a druid named Shara Rootheart. She
ruled over a small colony of followers, deep in the forest, where they
worshipped Amek, Lord of the Crows. She often led her followers in
sacrifice rituals and gave as much of herself as she could, cutting off
fingers and toes in honor of the dark lord. To show his pleasure, Amek
blessed Shara with this rough crown, allowing her to turn into a crow
and fly whenever she wished.

History: This circlet was worn by Amauris Laurantis, a famous sorcerer
known for hunting down and Killing dozens of dark-magic
necromancers. After he died, this circlet became the prized possession
of every magic user that wore it.
87. Circlet of Illusion

he followed his own illusion over a cliff to his death.

while in tree form, though they retain their hearing.
History: This circlet was created by a druid who was tired of being a
"human. She decided to spend some time as a tree on the riverbank, and
so she donned the crown and stood for four hundred years as a cherry
blossom tree. Every spring, she would drop pink petals into the river
and people would travel for miles to see her lovely visage. Finally, when
she'd decided she was done being a tree, she returned to her human
form and threw the circlet into the stream.

91. Glasses of Unobstructed Sight
Appearance: A pair of glasses with large, circular lenses made from
pink glass.
Enchantment: When these glasses are worn, the user can see through
walls up to a distance of sixty feet.
History: A famous treasure hunter, Leon Graves, wore these
noteworthy glasses on his adventures, using their magical abilities to
see secret doors and hidden treasures. Leon went missing just a few
years ago and was never seen again, though rumors of rival adventurers
and a brutal murder swept through the town when his iconic pink
glasses were found circling the black market.
92. Glasses of Metal Detection
Appearance: A rather old and scratched pair of glasses with thick,
smoked lenses.
Enchantment: While worn, all metal within sixty feet appears to glow
slightly, even through walls. The color of the glow will change
depending on the type of metal.
History: Many of these glasses were created for the dwarves in the
mountains, who used them to tunnel towards valuable metals. Some
were stolen to be used by thieves to scout victims, and others were used
by smiths to ensure perfect metal ratios. This pair was owned by Gronan
Stoneskin, a dwarf who was trapped and eventually killed by a cave-in
while mining gold.

illusions.

94. Glasses of Daysight
Appearance: A set of wire-rim glasses with oval lenses.
Enchantment: Gives the user perfect dark vision, though colors are
slightly distorted.
History: These glasses were worn by David Arkanov, a lamplighter in
the capital city. He lit the streetlamps for thirty years until, one fateful
evening, he was killed by a pair of thieves and his glasses stolen.
95. Vin's Telescoping Monocle
Appearance: A silver-rimmed monocle with three lenses layered over
one another.
Enchantment: Allows the user to ‘zoom-in’ the vision of one eye,
allowing them to clearly view things a mile away.
History: This monocle was worn by Vin, the captain of the King’s Watch.
The King's Watch patrolled the castle walls, monitoring the surrounding
countryside, guarding the king and keeping the townsfolk safe. When he
retired, he passed the monocle on to his successor.

what it was used to buy, where it was made, and so on.
History: This tongue piercing was created by Samantha May, a talented
and peculiar enchanter who had an interest in historical artifacts. No
ones sure why she chose licking as the method of her investigation, and
50 very few people chose to use this particular piece of jewelry.

101. Ever-Fresh Blouse
Appearance: A simple, finely-made blouse of white silk.
Enchantment: This shirt cannot be dirtied or stained, and always
carries the faint scent of soap. Any damage done to the shirt slowly heals
over the course of 1d4 hours,
History: Once there was a man named Dor'Orrin, who was a talented
tailor and enchanter. His clothing, which perfectly mixed style and
practicality, was highly sought-after by nobles and peasants alike. Now,
after his death, his clothing is even more highly valued.
102. Shirt of Steel Wool
Appearance: A loose long-sleeved shirt made from grey wool.
Enchantment: This shirt acts as a solid-steel cuirass.
History: Three of these shirts were created for each of the princess's
bodyguards. One day while traveling across the countryside, the
princess and her bodyguards were kidnapped and held for ransom. The
bodyguards were stripped of their weapons and armor but, through
sheer ferocity and force of wil, they managed to fight their way to
freedom with nothing but their bare hands, and spirited their princess
away to safety.

Appearance: A long-sleeved shirt made from red linen.
Enchantment: This shirt is completely fireproof.

shirt, which protected her from the worst of Sif blazing breath. The
battle was won, and Dai-Lin became a hero.

hunter. Leon went missing just a few years ago and was never seen
again, though rumors of rival treasure hunters and a possible murder
swept through the town when his iconic pocketed pants were found
circling the black market.

entranced by her beauty and talent and, years later, the two were
married.

world. No one was quite sure what became of the warrior after he fled

Enchantment: When these boots are worn, the user walks two inches

quicksand, broken glass, and can easily ignore difficult terrain, though
they cannot walk across water.
History: These boots were commissioned by a prince who wished to
walk through the world without dirtying his hem in the filth of the
commonwealth. The royal family was soon thrown out of the palace for
their cruelty and wasteful resource management.

burned into the soles.
Enchantment: These boots leave behind footprints that do not match
the character's weight, stride or shoe size. The print changes every one-
hundred steps, making it very difficult for the user to be followed.
History: Once, there was a famous poet named Daniel Kindried. His
works became so widely known that he was stalked by fans at every
turn. He wore these boots as part of an effort to slip into anonymity.

assassinate the duke of her homeland. The duke was a cruel man,
responsible for high taxes and terrible living conditions. He employed
cruel soldiers who took advantage of the townsfolk and, when one
careless soldier burned down Ida's tavern, she began to scheme.
145. Boots of Water Agility
Appearance: A pair of lightweight thigh-high boots made from a thin,
blue, scaled material.
Enchantment: While these boots are worn, the user becomes a talented
swimmer. They can swim at high speeds, hold their breath for long
periods of time, and can swim great distances without growing tired.
History: Long ago, rumors of a magical sea-monster rippled through the
little fishing town of Bass Bay. Lucian Balmer, a young fisherman with
ambitious dreams, saw the opportunity for fame and fortune and went
outin search of the mythical creature. After years of searching, he finally
caught sight of the sea-serpent and gave chase. After a battle that lasted
three days, the sea-serpent was slain, and its magical hide was forged
into a pair of boots.

Appearance: A pair of white leather boots with blue silk laces.
Enchantment: When the command word is uttered, the user floats one

History: These boots were worn by Artorius Icepalm, a prince who

Appearance: A pair of red leather boots with thin soles.

History: Many of these boots were created for the scouts and watch-
men of the king's army. They would sneak ahead of the army and report

Enchantment: The user can detect and identify any plant within 120ft.

the plants slowly wilt away back into the earth.
History: These boots were worn by Dora Mamora, the queen's head
gardener. She would use the boots’ magic to sense the health of the
plants, the moisture in the soil and the weeds that would sprout and
strangle the queen’s flowers.

Appearance: A huge cloak, made from the entire skin of a grizzly bear,

155. Ghost-Walk Cloak

Appearance: A shimmering, semi-translucent cloak made of a
mysterious lightweight material.

Enchantment: Once per day, the user can use the cloak’s magic to
become a spectral form for one hour. The user becomes intangible, and
they cannot interact with the material world. They can pass through
walls and cannot be seen by most living creatures, though some can
sense their cold presence.

History: Only six of these cloaks were ever made. They belonged to a

peace to those mourning their dead. They would wear these cloaks and
communicate with the deceased, passing along messages to the living.

History: This cloak was worn by Erika Belittle, the archmage of the

time. However, one day the chef washed his magic apron and hung it
outside to dry. To the chef's horror, the apron was stolen. Without its
magic, the restaurant soon closed.
195. Goggles of the Killer Glare
Appearance: A pair of leather goggles with tinted glass lenses
Enchantment: Three times per day, the user can scowl and shoot a
beam of bright red light from their eyes, causing 2d12 fire damage to a
creature within 60ft.
History: These goggles were worn by Omar O'Malley, an adventurer
who fainted at the sight of blood and refused to use any weapons that
would cause his enemies to bleed.

Appearance: A mask made from painted leather. It covers the upper

Enchantment: While worn, the user can examine someone and see, as

warrior of all, Samfeir, God of fighters and mercenaries. Samfeir won the
duel and, as punishment, cursed the warrior to wear this mask, so that
no one would recognize him for the legend he once was.

Enchantment: While worn, the user appears to be a living, semi-
translucent, amorphous shadow being with bright white eyes. The user
gains advantage on all intimidation checks.
History: No one is sure where this mask came from, or why it was made.
It simply appeared on the statue of the king in the city center. Three
days later, the king died of a heart attack.

History: Once there was a knight named Milly. She was a scout in the

by pirates. Many of the pirates were killed by young mages, however
many valuable tomes and tools were stolen. Bellam Mythweaver, a
young student, decided to dedicate his life to returning the stolen goods.
After a decade, he succeeded in finding ever single stolen artifact and,
to honor and repay him, the Academy gave him a suit of armor, crafted
from the bell that fell from the tower during the siege.

History: Any human-like being that wears this armor may find that it

251. Unmoving Cuirass
Appearance: A lightweight cuirass of hardened leather.
Enchantment: When the command word is spoken this cuirass freezes,
and cannot be moved from its place in space by any natural force.
History: This armor was created for a young warrior who was slight in
body and strength. He would often be shoved away by larger foes and,
to combat this, he commissioned this cuirass. His agility combined with
his expert timing allowed him to become one of the most fearsome
warriors in the land.
252. Cuirass of Soul-Following
Appearance: A silver cuirass etched with very faint runes. When the
magic is activated, the runes glow with white light.
Enchantment: After killing an enemy, the user can decide to follow the
deceased soul to the afterlife. Within two minutes of the creature's
death, the user can place one hand on the corpses head. The user's soul
will abandon their body, and follow the dead creature to its specific
afterlife, where the user can communicate with the dead soul, explore
the afterlife, etc, for one hour or until the user decides to return. The
user's body appears unconscious for the duration of their visit to the
afterlife. This cuirass must charge under the light of the full moon
between uses.
History: This armor was created for the purpose of questioning
prisoners and soldiers who died before interrogation; however, it was
quickly discovered that souls could not be threatened for information
in the afterlife. The cuirass was sold to the temple, who would use it
when an individual passed away quickly, without the opportunity to say
goodbye to their loved ones.

History: Once there was a woman named Gestelle. She was a legendary

for 1d10 rounds, or until the blood is scrubbed off.

immediately donned his gauntlets and climbed the dam. He worked for
three days and three nights, repairing and strengthening the dam. After,

hated her lessons, choosing to spend most of her time with the birds.
When people bothered her, she would simply send her ghostly eagles to
chase them away.

274. Gauntlets of Clear Sight
Appearance: A pair of gauntlets that seem to shift and change shape.
Sometimes they are leather gloves, embroidered with runes. Sometimes
they are silver, inlaid with ornate golden sigils. Sometimes they are
heavy gauntlets made from a strange, crystalline material.
Enchantment: When the user touches their thumbs and forefingers
together, they can peer through the formed triangle to see through all
illusions, including magical disguise, magical darkness, and so on.
History: These gauntlets were worn by the famous illusionist Winnie
Baz. She would use her powers for both combat and entertainment, and
her spells were so powerful that it was impossible to tell reality from
her illusions. Knowing the power such magic held, Winnie wore these
gauntlets so illusions could never be used against her.

281. Mechanical Greaves
Appearance: A pair of peculiar greaves made from brass. There are
stiff, jointed supports at the user's hips, knees and ankles, and the
occasional puff of steam billows from the mechanisms.
Enchantment: These mechanical greaves grant the user impressive leg
strength, allowing them to jump huge gaps, deadlift incredibly heavy
objects, kick down doors, etc. However, these greaves malfunction
when exposed to water. The bonuses return only after the mechanisms
have had plenty of time to dry.
History: These greaves were made by an enchanter who took an
interest in steam, and its peculiar ability to power his small, simple
machines. While he never wore this armor personally, he often hired
mercenaries to test his new mechanical armor in battle.
282. Greaves of Ease

Appearance: A pair of leather greaves painted with golden runes.
Enchantment: While worn, the user can move easily through rough
terrain, natural or magical.
History: These greaves were worn by Debias Crowsight, an apothecary
who was known for his rare and powerful medicines. He would
disappear into the wilderness for months on end, returning to his shop
without an apparent schedule.

305. Soul Blade

Appearance: A silver blade with a golden pommel wrapped in red silk.
Alarge ruby is set in the hilt, and it glimmers and shifts as if filled with

gem in the hilt of the sword. The user can communicate basic
information with the soul if the soul is willing. The souls of certain
creatures can also give the blade certain bonuses, at the game master’s
discretion. For example, a demons soul may cause the blade to grow a
ghostly claw that slash nearby foes; a necromancer’s soul may cause the
blade to revive slain enemies as enslaved undead, and so on.

blade in order to say prayers over the souls of evil creatures, blessing

them.

hunting lords for the king, he was crafting bows in his cabin in the
‘mountains.

Appearance: A short bow made from a strange black wood.

Appearance: A heavy bow made from a strange, flexible metal. It

340. Lightning Bow
Appearance: An ash longbow stained with a faintly blue oil.
Enchantment: Three times per day, the user can speak the command
word and fire a strange, glowing arrow. A rumbling begins in the sky

This enchantment can be used inside as well as outside.
History: This bow was crafted from the wood of the ancient God Tree,
an apple tree that stood at the top of the tallest mountain for thousands
of years, thriving despite the cold weather. Legend says it was the gods’
first gift to the earth, its apples feeding the first humans. It was
eventually struck by lightning and its wood made into many magical
artifacts.

horrible stone and took what metal he could, ignoring his impulse to
run. The mace he created oozed with the same evil aura that surrounded
the star.

Appearance: A gnarled staff made from blackened ash. Itis simple, but
the wood is soft and oiled to a faint shine, with a leather loop tied near
the top.
Enchantment: Three times per day, the user can utter the command
word and crack the staff on the floor, sending out a blast wave that does
2d12 damage to all creatures within ten feet, knocking them backwards.
History: This staff was made from the wood of an ancient tree that was
struck by lightning. Not wishing for the beautiful and ancient wood to
g0 to waste, a farmer crafted this beautiful staff without realizing the
magic it possessed.

364. Scepter of Miracles
Appearance: A papal scepter with a holy symbol mounted on the top.
Enchantment: This staff allows the user to perform minor ‘miracles’.
Once per day, the user can cast a minor 1d12 healing spell, as well as

365. Staff of Flight
Appearance: At first glance, this staff appears to be a tangled mess of
fabric, wood and twine. However, when the command word is uttered,
the staff pops out into an elegant glider.
Enchantment: When the command word is uttered, this staff forms into
a fully functional glider. A wind elemental has been sealed into the wood
and, once per day, the user can summon an updraft to launch them 60ft.
into the sky.
History: Once, there was a wizard who dreamed of flight. He enjoyed
changing into a falcon exploring the skies, but what he wanted more
than anything else was to share the joy of flight with his daughter. He
spent a decade perfecting the glider’s design to that his daughter might
fly with him someday.

366. Life-Sense Staff
Appearance: A long staff, blooming with leaves and flowers depending
on the time of year. Runes have been marked on the bark with white
paint.
Enchantment: When planted firmly in the ground, this staff allows the
user to sense all living creatures within 60ft. The user can also sense
their basic emotions and wellbeing through their connection to the
earth. Once per day, the user can hear and see through the eyes of one
living creature within 60ft. for ten minutes.
History: This staff belonged to Olly Wolf, a young hermit who was wise
beyond his years. He spent his time meditating in the mountains,
learning what he could from nature before writing his famous book of
poetry.

Enchantment: This staff is made from a very poisonous wood. All

History: Once, hundreds of years ago, there was a noble woman with a
passion for poisonous plants. She had a huge garden dedicated to the
deadly flora, and the Mahogany Poisonwood was one of her favorites.
However, one night, the young tree was stolen from her garden. Soon
after, an assassin known for his deadly poisonwood staff rose to fame.

368. Winter Staff
Appearance: A gray staff that is faintly cool to the touch. The ends glow
with a faint blue light.
Enchantment: Once per day, the user can slam this staff into the
ground, sending out a frozen, 30ft. shockwave. The temperature drops
to -10F and all water within the radius freezes solid. All creatures inside
the radius takes 1d6 frost damage per round unless properly dressed.
The spell lingers for ten minutes.
History: This staff was made by a wizard who wished to create a chilly
atmosphere for his wife, who was often too warm. His enchantment was
alittle too strong, however, and his first test of the staff resulted in both
him and his wife freezing solid.

would leave the safety of his tower.

371. Lightning Lance
Appearance: A steel spear that is crisscrossed with jagged, burned
lines. When held, electricity courses over the metal and harmlessly up
the user's arm.
Enchantment: All attacks with this spear do an additional 1d6 lightning
damage and, three times per day, the user can summon a lightning bolt
to strike down any target within 60ft. If the user is outside during a
thunderstorm, there is a 25% chance they will be struck by lightning.
History: This spear was carried by the captain of the queen's guard,
Mildred of the Glen, before her untimely death during the Battle of the
Third Kingdom.
372. Giant's Thorn
Appearance: A wickedly-sharp spear made from sturdy wood that has
been stained a deep burgundy. A number of needle-sharp thorns are
growing near the tip, and it seems to be surrounded by the faint scent
of citrus and iron.
Enchantment: This spear has advantage against any creature with
natural armor. The thorns on this spear are fragile, and have a 25%
chance of breaking off inside the enemy after a strike, doing 1d6 damage
per round until the thorn is removed.
History: Once, there was a giant who lived in the hills. On the top of the
hill grew a beautiful and massive and ancient orange tree. The giant
wanted nothing more than to pluck a single orange from the tree, but
when he tried, the dryad inside the tree chased him away. So, when the
dryad was washing her hair in the river, the giant tried again. He
reached out to pick an orange, but was rewarded only with a terrible
thorn driven deep into his finger. The dryad relented, seeing the giant's
sadness, and gave him an orange and sent him on his way. This spear
was made from the wood of the long-dead dryad.

373. Barb Lance
Appearance: A heavy lance with an oak handle, and a tip made from
fifteen barbs folded into one wickedly sharp point.
Enchantment: When the command word is uttered, the fifteen barbs
snap out of the spear’s tip, driving into the flesh of the creature it's
embedded in. The spear becomes completely stuck in the creature, and
cannot be removed without surgical intervention unless the command
word is spoken again.
History: This lance was the brutal invention of the kings brother,
Darnel, who loved nothing more than boar-hunting. He spent much of
his time tracking down the massive boars, and would often bring back
magnificent beasts for the winter feast. He crafted this spear so that
even if he did not strike a killing blow, the beast would not be able to
flee far. Prince Darnel was eventually gored in the stomach - a wound
that became infected and soon ended his life.

374. Golden Serpent Lance
Appearance: An elegant golden spear, etched with scales along its grip.
The tip of the spear is fashioned in the likeness of a darting snake, its
emerald fangs bared to strike.
Enchantment: Any creature struck by this spear takes an additional
1d6 acid damage from the poison that drips from the snake’s fangs.
When the command word is spoken, the spear becomes a living golden
serpent that will obey the user’s instructions.
History: This spear was the prized possession of Oculus Tenevault, a
mysterious and wise woman who lived a hundred years ago in a castle
along the coast. No one knows how she became so wise, but many would
visit her when they needed answers or advice. One day, she
disappeared, leaving nothing but her staff and a pile of clothing behind.

376. Firefrost Spear
Appearance: An ebony spear with blades on both ends. One blade is
silver and covered in a perpetual layer of tinkling frost. The second
blade is gold, shining with heat. Small glowing runes run along the grip.
Enchantment: Allows the user to choose which blade to strike with.
The golden blade does an additional 2d6 fire damage, while the silver
blade does an additional 2d6 frost damage. Once per day, the user can
either summon a freezing blizzard or a blistering sandstorm that lasts
ten minutes.
History: This spear was carried by Lusenfar, the demigod heir to the
god of fire. The other gods were infuriated by the half-god child and
banished him to the earth, but his father bestowed upon him the
Firefrost Spear so that, even as he walked alone in the world of mortals,
he would always be able to protect himself.

her deliveries, and so she grew this spear. Rumor had it that the florist
had dryad blood, because her flowers were more beautiful than any in
the kingdom.

upon an innocent audience member.

History: These gloves were crafted from the hide of a flame salamander

392. Sentient Venom Chain - Rosethorn
Appearance: A heavy ten-foot chain that is covered in viciously sharp
spikes. Venom drips ominously from the razor sharp points.
Enchantment: This chain is sentient, and goes by the name Rosethorn.
She is a cruel, bloodthirsty weapon, and will often kill or spare enemies
on a whim. She has an explosive temper, and will fly from the user's
hand to strangle any creature who doubts her power. All attacks do an
additional 1d6 poison damage. The chain will automatically wrap
around any enemy she’s thrown at, doing 1d6 piercing damage per
round until the chain is untangled.
History: This chain was enchanted by a gladiator, who wanted this
poison chain to act on its own. He did not realize that he'd given the
chain a personality, and was subsequently murdered by Rosethorn
‘when he suggested she wasn't truly alive.

Appearance: A heavy silver net, woven with razor-sharp blades.

History: Hundreds of years ago this net was carried by Saint Olimar

400. Automatic Slingshot
Appearance: A small, handheld artifact that appears to be a steel tube

Enchantment: After one minute of preparation, the user can aim this

incredibly high speeds towards the target. The bullet does 2d12
damage, but has a 10% chance of backfiring.
History: This strange device was carried by Captain Brawnston
Icewater, a pirate leader who spent his free time inventing and
perfecting his automatic slingshot. He carried a dozen of them into
battle, firing one after another before drawing his sword and charging
into the fray. He would often throw the guns aside, and lost many in the
roiling sea.

Appearance: A large, thick book bound in grey leather. The edges of the

remains in the trap.

451. Copycat Journals
Appearance: A set of two completely identical journals. They are bound
in burnished green leather, and each is emblazoned with an elegant fish
on the cover.
Enchantment: Anything written in one journal immediately appears in
the other.
History: Many of these journals were used as means of instant

twins who were sent to opposite sides of the world to be married. With
the use of these journals, they were able to talk to one another and

climbing onto the back of the prince's carriage, and he was quickly
hauled off to jail. The woman was ready with a plan to free him, but soon
decided she was better off without him and sailed away to a distant land.

safely harvest the tasty fruit. Many warriors use the seeds as explosive
projectiles, though they can be quite expensive to buy due to their
dangerous nature.

598. Quickrot Salt
Appearance: A handful of black salt in a small wooden pot. It has a
vaguely smoky scent.
Enchantment: When sprinkled on food, the food will quickly begin to
rot. Milk will go sour; bread will mold and meat will grow maggots in a

was purchased by a thief named Orion Delmise, who was planning on
robbing a duke’s household. What he was intending to do with the salt,
however, is unknown, as he was arrested before he could put his plan
into motion.

599. Always Spice

Appearance: A generous pinch of pale brown powder in a small paper
packet. It smells very faintly of cumin.
Enchantment: This spice can be sprinkled over food to prevent it from
spoiling. The food lasts three times as long as it would without the spice,
remaining perfectly edible until the magic fades.
History: This spice comes from roasted and ground leaves of the
Always flower, a rather unremarkable white flower that grows along
the road in the springtime.

600. Super Ragweed
Appearance: A handful of bright yellow florets in a cheesecloth bag. It
smells sweet, like fresh-cut grass.
Enchantment: For twelve hours after consuming this aromatic spice,
the user experiences terrible allergies including cough, runny nose,
itchy eyes and some difficulty breathing, however there is a 5% chance
that the consumer will not be affected.
History: This is a common plant that grows along the road along the
western coasts. Most people are allergic to this monstrous flower, and
many apothecaries offer magical allergy medication during pollen
season.

602. Odana’s Invisible Tripwire
Appearance: A long silver wire with two spikes on either end.
Enchantment: When anchored into the wall, this tripwire turns
invisible. While it is effective as a regular tripwire, it can also be
enchanted with a spell that will go off once the tripwire is triggered.
History: This tripwire was crafted by Odana Litherial, a wizard who
preferred to fight using invisibility, ranged spells and traps. Her short
career was cut short after she accidentally triggered one of her own
traps, bringing down an entire cave system around her.

may have flame wherever he goes.

deliver them safely and gently to the ground.
History: This harness was worn by Firella Linsen, a famous climber
who enjoyed nothing more than climbing the tallest cliffs in the
kingdom. Her husband, terrified for her safety, bought her this harness
so that she would always come home safely.

617. Everglade Waterskin
Appearance: A waterskin made from bright blue leather.
Enchantment: This waterskin is always filled to the brim with fresh
water, no matter how much the user consumes.
History: This waterskin was enchanted by Queeno Orpy, a wizard who
spent his life researching the plane of fire. She finally decided that she
could learn no more from the history books - she had to visit it herself.
She donned fireproof clothing and crafted the Everglade Waterskin, and
leapt into the plane of fire. After a week, she returned, singed but
unharmed. Her book on the subject became the leading academic study
guide.

advantage on all checks made to throw it, as it seems to fly almost
willingly towards the target. When the command word is spoken, the
hook will un-anchor itself and return to the user's hand.
History: This grappling hook was carried by Nassen Forrona, an
assassin and mercenary who was known for running jumping, climbing
and swinging through the capital city with the help of his magical
grappling hook.
619. Home-Again Compass

Enchantment: This compass will lead the user towards any place they
desire, as long as it is a place they have visited before. The user must
simply call out the name of the place, and the compass will lead them
directly there.
History: This compass was given to a young adventurer by his mother,
50 he could always find his way home.

621. Regrowth Candle
Appearance: An average, twelve-inch beeswax candle.
Enchantment: When the burned candle stub is left alone, it will slowly
begin to regrow, returning to full-size after one day of growth.
History: While a little pricy, folks often save up to purchase these
candles. Overall, it is a cheaper investment than constantly buying
candles. This one was bought by Linelle Orist, an artist who would often
paint late into the night.

622. Automatic Torch
Appearance: A simple wooden torch with a leather grip and a metal
cage on one end to keep the fuel in place.
Enchantment: This torch will light and extinguish automatically when
the user utters a simple command word. The torch can be ignited from
up to 60ft. away.
History: These torches can often be found in the cellars and dungeons
of rich lords and ladies. When they descend into the darkness, they can
simply utter the command phrase to lightall of the torches at once with
ease. This torch was stolen from a lord in the midwest, by a thief who
was discovered mid-heist and needed to make a quick getaway.

etched along the bottom.
Enchantment: After being lit, this lantern cannot be snuffed out by
water, wind or dust. It can’t run out of fuel, and will keep burning until
the user purposefully extinguishes the flame.

overboard and swam for two days with only this lantern to light his way
in the terrifying seas. He survived to tell the tale, and never set foot in
the ocean again.

626. Saint's Lantern

Appearance: A delicate golden lantern, set with pale opals and etched

with simple holy runes.

Enchantment: When lit, this lantern emits holy light that boils and

burns the skin of undead creatures, ghouls, demons, and those with
strong evil auras.

History: This lantern was carried by Saint Agnes, a priest who was
known for her stern motherly nature. She would walk the roads at night,
helping those she could while carrying this lantern to guide her. After
years of giving magical healing and holy blessings, her lantern became
a magical focus.

627. Lantern of Truth

Appearance: A lantern with walls made of thick panes of crystal.
Enchantment: When lit, the light cast by this lantern banishes all
untruths. All illusions illuminated by this lanturn sizzle and smoke
before fading away.

History: This lantern was carried by Sir Dally 0'Ron, an ancient witch
hunter who would search through the villages at night, ‘hunting for the
faintest whiff of witchcraft. His career was cut short when the women
of the town gathered together and drowned him in a horse trough.

628. Guilera’s Sunlight Lantern
Appearance: A spherical lantern made of gold, with sunlines etched
across the surface.
Enchantment: When lit, this light emits strong UV rays. Even short-
term exposure to this light causes painful burns and boils.
History: This lantern was originally developed by Princess Guilera, who
loved to grow plants, though none would grow in the dark palace. She
placed her plants under this strong light, and was delighted when they
flourished under its bright beam. After she passed, the lantern was
placed in the castle treasury.

631. Blanket of Warmth

Appearance: A heavy blanket of olive-green wool,

Enchantment: This blanket keeps the user warm, no matter the
weather.

History: This blanket was woven by an elderly man named Gerard
O'Rielly. He gave it to his grandson, who left to join the king's army. After
several years, he finally returned from the war and started a family of
his own, and he would tell heroic stories to his daughter under the same
blanket that kept him warm on the battlefield.

632. Breeze Blanket

Appearance: A light blanket made from several layers of pale blue
cotton.

Enchantment: This blanket keeps the user comfortable cool, no matter
the weather.

History: This blanket was woven by a woman who lived alone in the
desert, where she hunted for precious stones in the shallow caves. She
would use this blanket to keep herself cool in the hot desert nights, then
travel miles and miles to the nearest city to sell her wares.

patterns.
Enchantment: After falling asleep, the user and the blanket become
completely invisible until they wake.

onthe black market by a spell-blade who recognized its magic.

Appearance: A long, wrought-iron fire poker with a long pair of spikes
atone end.
Enchantment: The user can ignite flammable objects simply by placing
the fire poker against the desired object, and uttering the command
word.
History: This fire poker was purchased by Amalie Lorenso, the castle's
fire-starter. In the evening, when the sun began to set and a chill began
to settle over the cold stone castle, Amalie would methodically go
through each room and seta fire in the waiting fireplace. She was forced
to leave her job, however, when she accidentally set some curtains
ablaze.

647. Photo of Goldeen Smith - Sentient
Appearance: A small framed picture of a dirty man, covered in coal
dust. A pickaxe is clutched in one hand, and a ‘mining lantern is strapped

Enchantment: This picture seems to be alive. The man inside moves
and grins often, and will easily offer advice on caving, mining and
dungeoneering. He can accurately identify common minerals, and
seems very knowledgeable on everything he decides to comment on,
History: The man in this photo was Goldeen Smith, a man who spent
seventy of his ninety years working in a small coal mine. He loved
mining so much that, after he died, his soul refused to leave. Now he
spends his days inside this photograph, happily giving advice to miners
and adventurers alike.

History: These lighters, while uncommon, can be found all over the
kingdom. This one was owned by a ranger named Donovan Hues, an
adventurer who would often smoke his pipe as he walked along the
country roads.

Appearance: A rather dinged-up bucket made from tin. At the bottom,
arune has been hastily slathered on in white paint.
Enchantment: All water that is placed into this bucket becomes pure
and perfectly potable.
History: Many of these buckets were hastily crafted by a local hedge-
mage after a heavy rain flooded the town well with tainted water. The
mage was hailed as a hero, and now entertains a booming enchanting
business in the town that he helped through disaster.
650. Air Plant
Appearance: A leafy plant in a small terracotta pot.

coveted for its ability to purify the air. It can be found in many
households - it is easy to take care of and is quite hardy. This plant was

bad seasonal allergies.

651. Leafless Teapot
Appearance: A delicate, floral teapot made from white porcelain.
Enchantment: This teapot can make tea without tea leaves. The user
must simply add water, closes the lid and allow it to steep for three
minutes. It is a new type of tea every time, and it is always quite tasty.
History: This teapot was owned by Lady Doralia Whitehaven, an elderly
duchess who enjoyed nothing more than a good cup of tea. She would
often travel the world, searching out new and exotic varieties to try, and
eventually stumbled upon this enchanted teapot in a distant magical
market.
652. Forget-Me-Not Teacup
Appearance: A delicate, floral teacup rimmed with gold.
Enchantment: This teacup will keep tea, coffee, or any other beverages
hotand fresh until consumed.
History: This teacup was owned by a woman named Madeline Hale, a
scribe who would often make cups of tea only to forget about them
entirely, remembering them only when they were stone cold.
653. Ice Chest
Appearance: An iron box with heavy latches. Inside, the walls are
coated in ice and a heavy fog floats off the frozen surface.
Enchantment: The inside of this box is permanently frozen. Anything
placed inside this box will be kept very, very cold until removed.
History: This box was enchanted by a necromancer named Gornish
Garfield, who would often use it to store specimens until he was ready
to use them.

654. Bread Box
Appearance: A light, wooden box that is gently warm to the touch and
smells of freshly baked bread.
Enchantment: The inside of this box is humid and warm. Any food
placed inside will remain warm and fresh until removed.
History: This box was crafted by an enchanter for his wife, who would
spend long days working in the cornfields. He would often pack her
lunch, and wished he had a way to keep her food fresh and warm for
her. That sparked an idea in his mind, and he quickly made this lovely
box.
655. Fire-less Frypan
Appearance: A cast-iron pan with a fire rune etched on the bottom.
Enchantment: When the command word is spoken, the rune on the
bottom of this pan begins to glow with heat, allowing the user to cook
without a stove or fire.
History: This pan was owned by Grandma Pancake, a street vender who
was beloved by the locals. She would haul her cart into town in the early
morning and cook pancakes for all the hungry farmhands before they
went off to work. No one is sure what her real name actually is, or where
her magical pans came from.

on the blade near the handle.
Enchantment: This knife never dulls.
History: These knives are common in the restaurant industry, and are
often given as gifts. This knife in particular was originally owned by
Kusai Kimberly, the head chef of an ocean-side restaurant.

Appearance: A small wooden cutting board, laced with chopping

658. Ever Changing Spice Bag
Appearance: A tiny leather pouch that smells strongly of spices.
Enchantment: This pouch contains a tablespoon of spice that changes
every day at dawn. Spices can range from anything from salt, pepper or
paprika, to turmeric, graham marsala, or cocoa. There is a 10% chance
that it could be a magical spice - see page 252.
History: This spice bag was given to Winnie Lillith, a woman who loved

dream up recipes while performing her rather monotonous work. After
saving for years, she finally had enough to open a tiny restaurant that
quickly became the best restaurant in town.

and sealed, it will become a well-aged wine within two days.
History: This barrel was carried by Lewis Bernstein, a traveling
merchant who loved nothing more than a glass of wine after a hard day’s
work. It was tiresome to carry his wine collection with him, so he would
instead bring this barrel and experiment with recipes while traveling
from town to town.

red leather.

these pliers.

666. Axe of Harm
Appearance: A large woodcutter’s axe. A strange rune has been etched
into the iron blade.
Enchantment: No matter what this axe is used for, the user will almost
always hurt themselves with it before the day is done. Wounds can vary
from mild to severe, but blood is almost always drawn.
History: No one is sure where this axe came from or why it was made.
A young orphaned boy stole it from a cabin far out in the woods so that
he might cut himself firewood and protect himself, only to mortally
injure himself with it almost immediately. He stumbled to a temple
where the priests treated him and cast the cursed axe aside.

671. Sorcerer's Saddle
Appearance: A heavy, comfortable saddle made from a very dark
purple leather. Golden geometric designs trace the edges, and the
fastenings and buckles are made from intricately-worked gold.
Enchantment: This saddle surrounds the horse with invisible magical
armor, giving it strong armor class bonuses without impeding its
movement.
History: These saddles were used by of the many magic users in the
king's army. This saddle was owned by a warlock named Thimble
Tythes, a young man who joined the army in order to continue his
magical schooling. He made it through unscathed, however Tythes
refused to use magic after the War of the Two Rivers, during which
many sorcerers brutally killed each other.
672. Saddle Blanket of Comfort
Appearance: A heavy woolen saddle blanket, woven from cream-
colored yarn. Red and brown geometric designs have been woven into
the blanket, which is also speckled with flecks of dirt and hay.
Enchantment: This blanket will keep the horse at a comfortable
temperature, no matter the weather.
History: This blanket was owned by an old ranger who wandered the
wilds, taking down bandits and wolves and keeping the roads safe as
often as he could. He loved his horse more than anything in the world,
as she was his only friend during their lonesome travels. When she
finally passed, he spent three days burying her, and the old ranger left
her saddle and blanket on a stone over her faithful heart to mark her
place of rest.

691. Embroidery Life Thread
Appearance: A small basket filled with needles, thimbles and 1d20
spindles of brightly colored embroidery thread.
Enchantment: Anything embroidered with this thread seem to come to
life ~ birds will fly, flowers will sway in an invisible breeze, flames will
flicker and spark, moving over the fabric as if alive.
History: This embroidery thread was originally enchanted by a wizard
who had recently become a mother. She would sew small birds and
flowers into the hem of her dress, and the baby would spend hours
watching the little things dip and sway and flutter across the fabric
while her mother worked.
692. Spellwoven Thread
Appearance: A small tin box - inside is a heavy iron needle, a leather
thimble and 120 spindles of brightly colored embroidery thread.
Enchantment: This thread can be used to store spells, in the form of
embroidered images. The user can embroider as many spells as they
wish into their clothing instead of casting them, after which they can
cast them at any time without expending the spell slot.
History: This thread was used by a highborn assassin, who would stitch
her spells into her dress instead of a spellbook. They were easier to
sneak into parties and court occasions, allowing her to carefully and
quietly assassinate her target right under the noses of the other nobles.
693. Woodcarver's Blade
Appearance: An old, worn whittling knife with a slightly rusty blade.
Enchantment: Despite the rust on this blade, it cannot grow dull and it
will never slip and cut the user.
History: This blade was enchanted by a wizard who decided, after a
lifetime of sorcery in the service of the king, to retire. He spent his
remaining years on his back porch, whittling little statues of fantastical
creatures and giving them away to the local kids whenever they came
by.

###PAGE:309###
694. Perfectionist Chisel
Appearance: A delicate marble chisel made from a strange green metal,
with a simple sturdy handle.
Enchantment: This chisel will never chip too far or slip and make a
mistake in delicate stonework.
History: This chisel was crafted from the scale of a huge, ancient dragon
that was defeated after it attacked the capital city. Its massive body fell,
crushing the workshop of a humble sculptor. However, after making a
scale from its hide, he went on to make fantastically detailed sculptures
that spurred his name to fame.
695. No-Stick Sticky Glue
Appearance: A small glass bottle filled with thick paste. The lid is
difficult to get off.
Enchantment: This glue is incredibly sticky and very strong; however,
it will never stick to the user’s fingers.
History: Gallons of this glue was purchased by Sainsborough and Sons,
abookbinding company that specializes in the repair of old and decrepit
tomes. The delivery was waylald by highwaymen who were rather
disappointed to find that the huge caravan was carrying only glue, but
they stole what they could carry and sent the wagon on its way.
696. Sculpting Clay
Appearance: A 12x12 inch block of grey clay. It has the strong smell of
wet stone, and is quite firm.
Enchantment: The user can touch the clay, utter the command word
and then indicate anything within eyesight. The block of clay will begin
to shed small shavings and, after ten minutes, it will form into a nearly
perfect 3D recreation of the target.
History: Clay like this is quite cheap to buy, but most sculptors scoff at
the idea of using such magic. Instead, this clay is often used by those
who can't afford to hire an artist, usually to sculpt the face of a beloved
family member or pet.

697. Copycat Brush
Appearance: A paintbrush with short, fine bristles. The handle is made
from a pale wood, but it's barely visible beneath a coating of colorful
paint smears.
Enchantment: When set to a canvas or paper, the user can indicate any
painting within 15ft. The brush will set to work, darting around the page
ofits own volition. After twenty minutes, it will produce a fairly accurate
copy of the original artwork.
History: This brush was used by a woman named Stelezar Steel, a
famous art thief who stole hundreds of paintings during her long and
productive career. She eventually sold all of her paintings and retired,
but her legacy lived on. She was so famous that the copies she produced
are nearly as valuable as the originals.

700. Endless Paper

Enchantment: No matter how much paper is unspooled, it never seems

paper, appearing on the spool no matter how far from the forest it is.

701. Stasis Box
Appearance: A small, 12x12in. box made of dark wood with a swinging
lid and silver hinges.
Enchantment: Anything placed inside is frozen in time, remaining in
complete stasis until itis removed.
History: This box was carried by a traveling medic named Oinga Luan,
who would often place severed limbs inside this box until they could be
reattached.
702. Box of Unequal Dimensions
Appearance: A 10x12in. box made of red, polished wood.
Enchantment: On the inside, this box is three times as large.
History: Boxes such as this are often used by richer merchants, who use
them to easily transport large quantities of goods. This box was owned
by an elderly merchant named Yip Lissel, who was robbed along the
king's highway only a few months ago.
703. Unbreakable Chest
Appearance: A large, 2x3ft. box made of oak, with heavy iron bands and
hinges.
Enchantment: This box is indestructible.
History: This chest was owned by a duke name Lord Hellibor. He
seemed an average man, but he was ensconced in a tangle of dark magic.
He made many deals with terrible spirits to gain power, riches, women,
and eternal life. None of that helped him when a stray demon set fire to
his house, burning the whole place to the ground. This chest was the
only thing that still remained.

704. Animal Box

Appearance: A wooden 3x3ft. box made of rough wooden planks. Holes
have been drilled into the sides - the box occasionally rocks and emits
aterrible growl, as if a feral animal is trapped inside.

Enchantment: Despite the sounds, this box is entirely empty. It simply
emits frightening sounds, discouraging anyone from opening it.
History: This box was the clever invention of Dias Thrilpeak, a smuggler
who spent his days sneaking black-market goods from town to town.
The box rocks and yowls, and he would claim that the box contained a
rabid dog. Years passed without anyone suspecting his ruse, until he
stumbled across a guard he had met on the road before. Dias was
arrested, and his smuggling career prematurely ended.

705. Box of the Perfect Fit

Appearance: A 1x3ft. box made of sanded yew planks, with brass
hinges.

Enchantment: This box will shrink or expand up to 3ft. in any direction
to create a perfect fit for whatever is placed inside.

History: Boxes like this were often used by merchants who traveled
with delicate, fragile goods such as pottery or furniture.

706. Self-Lock Lockbox

Appearance: A small and elegant 6x10in. box, made of polished steel
with an inlay of gems.

Enchantment: When something is placed inside this box and the lid is
shut, it can only be opened again by the person who placed the item
inside. After the item is removed, it can be opened by anyone until
another item is placed inside.
History: This box was carried by a silversmith, who would often make
deliveries to noble households across the city. He was robbed many
times, but the thieves were never able to get the chest open before they
were tracked down by the city guard.
