708. Box of Need

Appearance: A 6x10in. box made from polished, dark mahogany with
golden hinges.

Enchantment: Once per week, the user can place their hand on the box
and summon any non-magical item they have dire need of, such as rope,
candles, blankets, food, and so on. Gold and jewels cannot be
summoned, though silver or copper coins will appear when needed. As
long as it can fit in the box, it will appear.

History: This box was the subject of many legends. Some say there was
a blessed woman who walked the roads hundreds of years ago, giving
away everything she had. A god, seeing the woman's kindness, gave her
this box of blessings so that she would never want for anything,

709. Lead-Lined Box

Appearance: A heavy 12x12in. box made of thick oak planks. Inside, the
box is lined with a dull metal.

Enchantment: This box can safely store anything. Fire, acid, magic -
this box is impenetrable on the inside.

History: This box was used by a traveling alchemist who would often
walk the roads with a collection of dangerous, volatile chemicals. This
box and its magic saved his life on many occasions, when caustic or
explosive chemicals came into contact with one another.

popular by her devious wooden puzzles and uniquely designed
furniture.

Enchantment: A new, different and sometimes exotic alcohol appears
in the bottle once per day.
History: This bottle was a gift to a noble, who was known in his circle
of friends to have a taste for drinking. Because of its ornate bottle, it was
stolen when the house was broken into.

heal the body. If they were successful, the soul would return to the body
~ if they failed, the soul would be ritually released into the afterlife.

753. Banshee Bottle
Appearance: A plain glass bottle with mist swirling inside. Occasionally

golden wax.
Enchantment: This bottle contains the sealed spirit of a banshee. When

754. Bottle of Silence
Appearance: A small spherical bottle made of glass with ornate gold
detailing.
Enchantment: The user can indicate a target within 20ft, and utter the
command word. The target becomes silenced as their voice becomes
sealed in the bottle. Anything they attempt to say can be very faintly
heard inside the bottle. This bottle can be used once per day, and the
effects last for ten minutes.
History: This bottle was kept in the king's court, and used to silence
courtiers who could not hold their tongues. When the king passed and
the prince rose to the throne, he had the bottle removed from the court
as he believed it to be in poor taste.

755. Storm Bottle

Appearance: A large spherical bottle with a golden cap. Inside, tiny
bolts of lightning stab out of roiling clouds.

Enchantment: When the lid is removed or the bottle is broken, a
terrible thunderstorm flows up into the sky. The storm will rage for 1d6
hours, with heavy rain and frequent lightning. If opened inside, the
storm will fil the available space.

History: Once, many years ago, a drought swept across the land. An
enchanter crafted a few of these storm bottles for farmers and
gardeners whose livelihoods depended on frequent rain.

756. Fireball Cocktail

Appearance: A whiskey bottle half-full of an amber, caustic-smelling
alcohol. A cloth tag has been shoved into the mouth of the bottle and
sealed with wax.

Enchantment: When the tag is lit and the bottle thrown, the cocktail
will explode into a sticky fireball on impact. It sticks to the target, and
burns violently for five minutes.

History: This cocktail was originally intended to be a tasty drink, but
the bartender soon realized it was too volatile for those with even the
strongest constitutions. Troublemakers and mercenaries continued to
purchase bottles of the stuff, but few of them intended to drink the brew.

757. Pigeon Bottle

Appearance: Along narrow bottle made of weather-beaten blue glass.
Enchantment: When a piece of paper is placed into the bottle, the user
can speak the name of someone they know. The paper message will
disappear with aloud ‘pop’, and appear in front of the chosen individual,
no matter how far away they happen to be.

History: Bottles such as these are often used by nobles and
businessmen who need a reliable and secretive way to send messages.
‘This bottle was owned by a duke named Bellum Groosh, a man who was
eventually arrested for conspiracy.

passed over the land.

the warrior a jar as thanks.

gather flaming-hot specimens that would shatter any other vessel.

771. Scabbard of Cleaning
Appearance: A sheath made of dark blue leather, with silver detailing.
Enchantment: No matter how dirty the sword is, it is automatically
cleaned to a polished shine when sheathed.
History: This scabbard was carried by famous headhunter and
mercenary, Filamena Fitsgivens, who would often forget to clean her
blade after cutting off the heads of her victims. After she retired, she
bestowed her sword and Scabbard of Cleaning upon her beloved
granddaughter, who wanted to become a caravan guard when she grew
up.
772. Bard's Band Case

Appearance: A violin case made from fine black leather, with silver
latches.
Enchantment: This small violin case can magically carry up to five
instruments of any size.
History: This case was created by a bard named John Songwriter, who
traveled with a band of four other musicians. They lived a merry life,
traveling from inn to inn with nothing but their horses and a single
violin case that carried all of their instruments. The five, who were
known as the Damned Five, were devastated when the magical case and
all of their instruments were stolen.

Enchantment: Any instrument placed into this case will be magically
and perfectly tuned.
History: This case was carried by a proud bard named Finbar Boar, who

one day, he decided to spend the night in an inn, only to discover the
queen herself was residing there. He whipped out his instrument and
struck up a tune that pleased her so much, he was immediately hired as
a court musician.

History: This scabbard was carried by Girard Holst, a mercenary who

779. Quiver of the Elements
Appearance: A quiver decorated with silver fittings. Three gems of
yellow, blue and red have been fit in ornate settings around the top.
Enchantment: The three gems correspond to the elements fire, frost
and lightning. Once per day, the user can switch between these
elemental stones. Depending on which stone is chosen, the quiver will
imbue the arrows with an additional 1d6 fire, frost or electric damage.
History: Long ago, there was a warlock who learned how to crystalize
magic. Her name has been lost to time, but she made many of these
crystals throughout her life, many of which were used to enchant
objects such as this quiver. Due to their rather volatile nature, the
warlocK’s life was cut short in a magical accident, and many of the
crystals have been lost.

781. Waterproof Scroll Case

782. Locking Scroll Case
Appearance: A heavy leather scroll case, reinforced with steel ribs.
Enchantment: This scroll case can be locked. When the command word

History: This scroll case was carried by Alfie Wolfson, the king's
messenger. It was a frightening job, as these messengers were often
kidnapped and tortured until they opened the case. However. Alfie was
a staunch servant and perished rather than give up the king’s valuable

Appearance: A mahogany writing case, filled with blank paper, pens
and pots of ink.
Enchantment: When the command word is uttered, this writing case

spoken again, it will pop into existence in front of the attuned user.
History: This case was carried by Saint Ubar Den, a scribe who would

everyone, even those who could not afford it. After he was murdered on

784. Dimensional Scabbard

known far and wide for her just and noble ways. She and her company
of soldiers would rescue men, women and children in abusive or
dangerous situations, protecting them until they were ready to make it
on their own. Lady Sunset never carried her blade at her side, to avoid
frightening or provoking people unnecessarily.

Enchantment: Any knife or dagger placed in this sheath will remain

800. Basket of Gold-Finding
Appearance: A wide gold panning basket made from loosely woven
wire.
Enchantment: Anything invaluable placed in this basket, such as sand,
lead or imitation gold, simply falls through the bottom, leaving only real
precious metals and gems behind.
History: These baskets are most often seen in banks, allowing them to
test the validity of coins and gems. However, this basket was owned by
a gold-hunter named Dobias Smitten, who dedicated his life to
becoming rich. He spent years panning the mineral-rich rivers of the
south. For most of his life, he found nothing, Then, one day, he
miraculously panned a fistful of diamonds. Immediately he sold all of
his mining supplies and bought a manor, where he lived happily for the
rest of his days.

Enchantment: When the command word is spoken, this stuffed cat

History: This cat once belonged to a wizard named Fednaw. He was an

enchantment but, after his beloved cat passed away, he began to dabble
in necromancy. He combined the two magics to bring a semblance of life
back into his dear friend.

Appearance: A small gem in a velvet-lined box.

changes with the sun.

Enchantment: When the lid is opened, a minty and energizing mist
gently floats out the top. Anyone who inhales this mist feels instantly
refreshed.
History: Mist vials such as this can often be seen clutched in the hands
of nobies as they stroll through town in the summer, when the stench
can be rather overpowering. It can also be used to revive swooning
individuals, and ease the symptoms of heat stroke. This vial was owned
bya noble man named Gregor Hones, who was quite sensitive to the full
heat of summer.

[v 901. Fire Lyre
Appearance: A lyre made from vibrant redwood, with golden strings.
Enchantment: When played, the user can control small flames with the
ebb and flow of their music.
History: This lyre was carved from the trunk of the Fire Wood Tree, a
huge redwood that was the largest tree in the kingdom. When a fire tore
through the forest, the weakened tree fell to the ground. Mourning the
loss of such a noble giant, a woodcarver fashioned its body into this lyre.

902. Abigail's Lute of Inspiration
Appearance: A lute made from pale wood, with small mother of pearl
runes set into the frets.
Enchantment: When this lute is played, all allies within earshot gain
+1d4 to their 20 rolls.
History: This lute belonged to Abigail Finch, a beloved bard who
traveled the world, writing songs and delving deep into dangerous
dungeons.
903. Unsettling Hurdy Gurdy
Appearance: A rather large hurdy gurdy that has been painted with
dull, clashing colors.
Enchantment: This hurdy gurdy is always slightly off-tune. Its music is
decidedly off-putting, and anyone who hears it becomes very unsettled.
History: No one knows where this object came from, or why it came to
be.

904. Piercing Violin
Appearance: A violin made from a dark wood. Its fittings are gold, and
the strings are brightly silver.
Enchantment: Three times per day, the user can strike a piercing note
on this violin. Everyone within earshot takes 2d6 piercing damage, and
will begin to bleed from their ears.
History: This violin was owned by Davis irard, a battle bard known for
his violent music. His music could please, or deafen. His tunes could be
danced to, or fought with. His melodies had many ways of bringing tears
to peoples’ eyes.
905. Thunder Drums
Appearance: A set of small drums, made from dark leather and pale
wood. Golden runes have been set into the wood.
Enchantment: Once per day, the user can pound on the drums, emitting
a tumultuous thunder and causing lightning to strike a single target for
3d12 damage.
History: This drum was made from the rare Steelwood - a wood so hard
thatit is nearly impossible to cut, let alone carve. This drum was carved
using powerful spells over a hundred years ago, and has been carried
by many bards since.
906. Perfect Tune Mandolin
Appearance: A mandolin, made from blue-gray wood with silver frets.
Enchantment: This mandolin is always perfectly in-tune.
History: This mandolin was carried by a bard named Frederic Bean,
who was always ready and willing to strike up a tune for anyone who
had a fancy to listen.

921. Half-Finished Wand
Appearance: A yew stick, half carved into an elegant wand.
Enchantment: This wand was originally intended to enhance the user's
magic. The user has a 50% chance of doing twice the damage. However,
if they fail, the enhanced spell backfires and the user takes the damage
instead.
History: Once, there was a famous wandmaker named Ged Geronius.
He had a small shop on the road between the capital city and the sea,
and wizards came from all over the world to buy his wares. This wand,
however, wasn't even finished before it was stolen by a young girl who
was determined to run away from home and become a magician. Things
didn't end well.
922. Seer’s Crystal Ball
Appearance: A sphere made from cloudy crystal, with a stand made
from ebony and red velvet.
Enchantment: Anyone who gazes into the ball has a 10% chance of
seeing a vision of their future.
History: This crystal ball belonged to a talented fortune-teller by the
name of Holston Bower, who lived hundreds of years ago. Many believe
him to be the most accurate seer of all time, and nobles and kings, lords
and ladies would seek out his sage wisdom. After he foresaw his own
death, he sold everything he owned and spent the rest of his life in
luxury on the southern coast.

925. Isolate Gloves
Appearance: A pair of thin, silken gloves with runes of negation
embroidered into the hem.
Enchantment: These gloves do not conduct magic. Magic cannot pass
through the gloves, neither from the inside nor the outside.
History: These gloves were worn by a noble woman who was secretly
the daughter of a red dragon. Her magic was innate and, because she
was not taught, she could not control it. Instead of struggling to control
the flames that often flared from her fingertips, she decided to wear
these gloves, day and night.

Appearance: An empty glass sphere, with a small golden hatch on one
side.
Enchantment: The user can expend spell slots, filling this orb with up

which, all spells are cast at once.
History: Many of these spheres were used in the holy wars. They were
handed out to soldiers, who would pelt the opposing armies with spell
bombs. Few remain intact, making them expensive and rare.

northern village. She was an eleventh-generation herbalist, and her
shop was many of hundreds of years old. One day, she decided she'd had
enough herbalism, and sold her shop to pursue her dreams as a bard.

IT 941. Saint Armund'’s Rice
Appearance: A single grain of rice in an ornate glass and gold vial.
Enchantment: Though this grain of rice registers as faintly magical, it
does not appear to be enchanted.
History: This grain of rice was the first grain harvested after ten years
of drought. Saint Armund came to the suffering land, and wept tears of
sorrow on the dry soil. Inmediately, rainclouds filled the sky and wept
with the Saint, and the land was dry no more.
942. Amulet of Gold
Appearance: A simple holy sigil on a chain.
Enchantment: This amulet carries a strong holy aura. It will burn the
skin of any demon that lays hands upon it.
History: This amulet was kept safe by the Priests of the Valley, who
claim that a goddess came down from the sky and blessed this amulet
herself.
943. Saint Dahlia’s Teeth
Appearance: A set of real human teeth embedded in a heavy, golden
skull
Enchantment: Anyone who holds this skull is cannot tell a lie.
History: These teeth belonged to a woman named Dahlia Buds, a
priestess who was known to be able to settle any dispute. She could see
to the heart of all matters, and truth arose around her like flowers in the
springtime. After her death, she was declared a saint and her teeth were
entombed in this golden skull.
389

----------------------

###PAGE:399###
944. Finger of King Howler
Appearance: A gnarled, wrinkled finger in a decorative jar. A large
signet ring is stuck on the shriveled finger.
Enchantment: This object does not appear to be enchanted.
History: This finger belonged to King Howler III, who sat on the throne
hundreds of years ago. He was quick to anger, and it was common belief
that anyone he pointed at would be immediately beheaded. When he
was dethroned by an angry mob, he was beheaded and his chopped off
his finger. Legend has it that, if the amputated finger points at someone,
they will die within three days.
945. Blood of the Sun God
Appearance: A heavy, ornate vial with a smear of dried blood inside.
Enchantment: Though this vial registers as faintly magical, it does not
appear to be enchanted.
History: Once, there was a handsome man named Claro. He simply
showed up in town one day, offering aid where he could and laughing
merrily with the townsfolk. No one knew where the lad came from, but
his presence was a blessing to the town. Many believed him to be the
mortal form of the sun god, though no one can say where these rumors
started.
946. Weeping Goddess
Appearance: A six-inch statue of a goddess, carved from aged ivory.
Enchantment: Tears will pour from the eyes of this statuette whenever
itis within one 100ft. of an unholy creature.
History: This statue depicts the goddess of the moon; the goddess of
purity of heart and intention. The statuette first began to weep when a
man came to the temple, begging to be accepted as a priest. The
statuette wept in his presence, and the priest refused the man. Ever
since that day, new initiates were required to kiss the statuette before
they were allowed a priesthood.

###PAGE:400###
947. Knife of Saint Bordin’s Blood
Appearance: An incredibly old kitchen knife. Occasionally, a drop of
blood will drip down the blade.
Enchantment: Anyone injured by this blade has a 25% chance of being
immediately stricken with a terrible fever.
History: Once, there was a priest named Bordin. He was diligent and
learned, but one day he fell terribly ill. His fever caused him terrible
hallucinations, and during one particularly violent vision, he took up a
knife and struck the cleric who was treating him. The other priests were
horrified at first, then amazed when the cleric shimmered, revealing his
true demonic form. Bordin eventually recovered, and was declared a
saint.
948. Heads Up Coin

Appearance: An ancient golden coin.
Enchantment: This coin always lands heads up.
History: Once, a god walked the earth in the form of a beggar. Everyone
passed him by without giving him a second glance, except for one
woman - a young lady who tool pity on the disheveled man. She gave
him the only coin she had and the god smiled, and blessed the woman.
Priests believe this is that very coin.

950. Goblet of Ash - Cursed
Appearance: An ornate silver goblet, set with a dozen rubies and as
‘many diamonds.
Enchantment: Anyone who drinks out of this goblet will be cursed.
From then on, everything they eat or drink will crumble to ash in their
mouths until the curse is removed.
History: This was the chalice of a proud and vile king. He believed his
reign to be perfect, though thousands of citizens starved every day.
Innocent men were imprisoned, and crooked tax collectors roamed the
land bearing his name. Then a god came to him and cursed him. As long
as he was king, everything would turn to ash in his mouth and he would
feel the hunger of his people. The king held on for four days until he
relented, and gave up the crown.
951. Bread of Plenty
Appearance: A greasy, dusty crust of bread in an ornate glass box,
decorated with golden vines and ruby flowers.
Enchantment: Though this bread registers as faintly magical, it does
not appear to be enchanted.
History: Nine hundred years ago, the kingdom was starving. Droughts
wracked the lands, and nothing would grow. The plants were dead and
the animals were dying. The kingdom was wasting away. Taking pity on
the mournful people, a god descended from the heavens and gave to
each citizen aloaf of dark bread. They ate and were full, and it gave them
the strength they needed to survive the oncoming days of drought.
When the rains finally came, the people rejoiced and gave thanks.

953. Lock of Saint Oberias
Appearance: A lock of white hair in a silver locket, etched with holy
symbols.
Enchantment: Anyone who wears this locket is immune to fire damage.
History: Once, there was a priest named brother Oberias. One day, he
was walking down the road when he saw a house in flames. Hearing
screaming from inside, he charged into the flames without care for his
own safety. Everyone believed him dead; however, moments later he
emerged from the flames with a child in his arms. His clothes were
burned away and his skin was caked in smoke, but he and the child were
completely untouched by the flames.

954. Gaius's Glasses
Appearance: An ancient pair of round-rimmed glasses with scratched
lenses.
Enchantment: This object does not appear to be enchanted.
History: Once, many of hundreds of years ago, there was a man named
Gaius. He was a scribe, and his eyes often troubled him. Finally, he could
no longer read, nor see well enough to write. He prayed to the gods to
give him back his sight, so he may continue his work. Legend says that
a woman came to him, and removed these glasses from his face. She
kissed him on the forehead and, in that moment, his eyesight was
returned to him.
955. Bowl of Need
Appearance: An ancient wooden bowl.
Enchantment: When held, the bowl can sense what the user truly
needs. If itis something simple and nonmagical, such as a bowl of soup
ora needle and thread, it appears quietly in the bottom of the bowl, as
ifithas been there all along.
History: Once, there was a beggar who was sitting along the city streets.
He was gaunt and hungry, and had nothing but a wooden bowl to his
name. A goddess was walking along the road - seeing the beggar's
suffering, the goddess touched the bowl with one elegant finger. It filled
‘with hearty soup, and the beggar never went hungry again.
956. Holy Water
Appearance: Alarge bottle of holy water with a golden cap. Aloose holy
sigil sits in the bottom of the bottle.
Enchantment: A simple vial of holy water.
History: Holy water can be purchased at almost any church or temple.
This ornate bottle was carried by Godiva Dahl, a superstitious noble
woman who was known for constantly crossing herself with holy water.

958. Book of the Unholy Prince
Appearance: A large, ancient book that looks as if it may fall apart at

the pages are covered in archaic and crammed sigils. It appears to be

Prince - priests have been trying to destroy this book for hundreds of

Appearance: An archaic brass oil lamp, with a small blue flame
flickering inside.

be the end of the world. The priests lit an oil lamp and prayed - to their
awe, the lamp never went out. Two days later, the sun re-emerged and
the lamp was left to burn for all eternity.

960. Laurels of Saint Ivy
Appearance: A laurel wreath made from holly and ivy.
Enchantment: This wreath preserves the body of whoever wears it. If
the user is alive, they will age half as quickly. If the wearer is dead, the
corpse will not spoil.
History: When a head priestess named sister Ivy passed away, her body
was entombed beneath the temple. Thirty years later, the priests
opened the tomb to check on her, and they were amazed to find her
body completely intact. Her corpse was as fresh as the day she died, and
she was declared a saint for this miracle.

964. Liar's Leaves
Appearance: Ten healthy green oak leaves in a small bag.

History: Liar's leaves are an ancient magic used by the people of the
temperate southern islands. When someone was suspected of
committing a crime, they were brought before an elder and a liar's leaf
placed into their hand. If they were honest in their innocence, they were
released. If they were lying, they would be punished appropriately.

awareness of the world around them.

Enchantment: These dice have an 80% chance of rolling sevens.

972. Honest Cards

Appearance: A set of playing cards, with the image of a winking sun on
the back of each card.

Enchantment: These cards cannot be used to cheat, no matter how
hard one tries.

History: These cards are commonly found in large gambling dens to
keep the players honest.

973. Tarot Cards
Appearance: A set of well-worn and beautifully illustrated tarot cards.
Enchantment: Once per day, the user can randomly draw a tarot card.
The card drawn will somehow indicate the user's future.
History: These cards were owned by Madame Onarra Sigh, an elderly
fortune-teller who owned a shop along the west-coast docks. After
many years of telling fortunes, she drew The Tower. Understanding
what that meant, she passed her shop on to her apprentice and died in
a terrible accident the next day.

them to get a grasp of their location no matter the conditions.

Pride, that often sailed along tropical, rainy coastlines.

be.
989. Cyclical Compass
Appearance: A sturdy, finely made compass. The needle simply spins
in circles at varying speeds.
Enchantment: This object does not appear to be enchanted.
History: No one knows where this object came from, or why it came to
be.
990. Perfect Sense Compass
Appearance: A simple, elegant silver compass.
Enchantment: While this compass is on the user's person, they will
‘have a perfect and consistent sense of direction.
History: This compass was given as a gift to the son of a lord. The boy
had a terrible sense of direction, and was constantly getting lost even in
the familiar streets of his home city. Partly practical, partly prank, his
father had this compass enchanted for the boy's birthday.
406

----------------------

###PAGE:416###
Furniture
[Ne
— Pra 0}

991. Foldable Bed
Appearance: A small wooden cube. When activated, it appears to be a
large, luxurious four-poster bed.
Enchantment: At first, this item appears to be a small wooden cube.
When the command word is spoken, it quickly inflates into a large,
heavy, beautiful four poster bed. When the command word is uttered
again, the bed returns to its small cube form.
History: These items were created for nobles who were forced to travel
long distances or spend a lot of time on the road, so they would never
be without their creature comforts.

5 Ls
992. Pet Fence
Appearance: A folded, foot-tall high fence made of golden wire.
Enchantment: Common, non-sapient creatures cannot pass over this
small golden fence. An invisible wall of magic seems to prevent them
from going over, no matter how hard they try.
History: This fence was commissioned by a noble, who loved nothing
more than his tiny, pampered, perfectly-bratty dog. He would take the
pup out on trips to the countryside, where he would set up this little
fence and allow the dog to roll around in the fresh grass to her little
heart's content.
407

994, Folding Table
Appearance: A small wooden cube. When activated, it appears to be a
large dining table made from beautifully polished mahogany. The
surface of the table is a little scratched, and circular burn marks mar the
otherwise perfect surface.
Enchantment: At first, We

408

----------------------

###PAGE:418###
995. Chest of Hunger

Appearance: A large chest made from polished oak, with heavy silver

latches. A faint growling, like that of a dog, seems to emanate from

inside.

Enchantment: When this chest is opened, the user can clearly see two

sets of sharp teeth along the edges of this chest. If the chest is opened

by someone unfamiliar, it will attempt to bite them. The user must feed
the chest meat or blood on a regular basis in order to gain its favor.
History: This chest was designed by an elderly wizard, who was very
afraid of his apprentices stealing his most valuable secrets.

996. Armchair of Easy Passing

Appearance: A soft armchair that looks incredibly comfortable and
incredibly inviting.

Enchantment: Anyone who sees this chair must roll a will save, or else
they will feel compelled to sit down. Once seated, they quickly become
sleepy and peaceful as the armchair slowly, ever so slowly, starts to
consume them. After one hour, the user will be completely consumed. If
another person attempts to remove the sleeping user from the chair,
they will find that the user's skin has adhered to the surface of the
armchair.

History: No one knows where this object came from, or why it came to
be.

997. Following Stool
Appearance: An ornately upholstered stool made from polished oak.
Enchantment: This stool will squeak and yip like a small dog as it walks
behind the user at a respectful distance. The user can utter the
command word, causing the stool to sit, stay, follow, or come closer.
History: This stool was owned by Rognar Booth, a noble who tired easy
and often needed to sit down. This stool would follow him everywhere
he went, even out into town.
409

----------------------

###PAGE:419###
998. Study Lamp
Appearance: A table lamp with a colorful glass shade.
Enchantment: When the command word is uttered, this lamp will float
gently off the table and follow just behind the user's shoulder, casting
light on them wherever they go.
History: A few of these lamps can still be found in the royal library,
where they are often used by those studying or working late through
the night.
999. Clap Lamp
Appearance: A seemingly simple oil lamp with a colorful glass shade.
Enchantment: The user must simply clap twice to lit or extinguish this
lamp.
History: These lamps are exceptionally popular among the aged lords
and ladies, who disliked getting out of the warm safety of bed to
extinguish candles before bed.
1000. Dimensional Drawers
Appearance: A chest of drawers made from polished ebony, inlaid with
mother-of-pearl runes.
Enchantment: This chest of drawers reeks of dimensional magic. When
the attuned user snaps, the drawers and everything inside disappear
into a bubble dimension, where they are safe from all but the most
powerful dimension hoppers. When the user snaps again, the drawers
pop into existence right in front of them.
History: These drawers were enchanted by a very powerful warlock,
who drifted through dimensions like a bird drifting through clouds. He
needed a way to keep all of his possessions close at hand, and spent two
years crafting this incredibly magical, incredibly volatile, incredibly
expensive chest of drawers.

###PAGE:422###
About the Author
Madeline Hale was born on the west coast of Michigan during the
coldest part of the year. She spent her childhood in the snow, and began
traveling at a very young age. To avoid the hitmen. You know how it is.
She was introduced to D&D at the tender age of twelve, and her art
career began soon after. Now, she’s been drawing for a decade and
writing books for just as long. Madeline enjoys tabletop games, video
games, board games, chocolate, and petting dogs - though, she finds
writing about herself in third person to be a very unsettling experience.

Ifyou enjoyed ‘Arcane Objects and Curious Curios’, check out
Madeline's other tabletop gaming books on Amazon.com.
Table Fables: A Collection of Tables for the Weary Game Master
Table Fables II: The World-Builder’s Handbook
The Adventures Of: Record Keeping for Game Masters
Ifyou would like to keep up with Madeline's latest projects, visit us at
www.madelinehaleart.com.
Thanks for reading and happy gaming.
